#### Round 13  [stage=-]
- think_tool:
  > Excellent! Now I can see the full trace call chain for a failed request:
  > 
  > **Call Chain (trace: 50b3710d4ab34d07293d75c3457b6ced)**:
  > ```
  > loadgenerator → POST /api/v1/travelplanservice/travelPlan/quickest [ERROR 500]
  >   → ts-ui-dashboard → POST /api/v1/travelplanservice/travelPlan/quickest [ERROR 500]
  >     → ts-travel-plan-service → POST /api/v1/travelplanservice/travelPlan/quickest [ERROR 500]
  >       → ts-travel-plan-service → TravelPlanController.getByQuickest [ERROR]
  >         → ts-travel-plan-service → POST [ERROR 500]  ← calling route-plan-service
  >           → ts-route-plan-service → POST /api/v1/routeplanservice/routePlan/quickestRoute [ERROR 500]
  >             → ts-route-plan-service → RoutePlanController.getQuickestRoutes [ERROR]
  >               → ts-route-plan-service → POST [ERROR 500]  ← calling travel-service
  >                 → ts-travel-service → POST /api/v1/travelservice/trips/left [ERROR 500]
  >                   → ts-travel-service → TravelController.queryInfo [ERROR]
  >                     → ts-travel-service → TripRepository.findAll [Unset] (ok)
  >                     → ts-travel-service → POST [Error] ← this is calling something!
  > ```
  > 
  > So the call chain is:
  > **loadgenerator → ts-ui-dashboard → ts-travel-plan-service → ts-route-plan-service → ts-travel-service**
  > 
  > Now the key question is: inside TravelController.queryInfo, there's a "POST" span with ERROR status. This is ts-travel-service calling another service. But what service does it call?
  > 
  > Also the TripRepository.findAll succeeded (Unset = OK). So ts-travel-service CAN access the database but is failing when calling another service.
  > 
  > The span `21d761be872cf8e4` shows:
  > - service: ts-travel-service
  > - span_name: POST
  > - attr_status_code: Error
  > - attr_http_response_status_code: null (no HTTP code recorded)
  > 
  > This is the critical span. It's ts-travel-service making a POST call internally that's failing. Let me look at what URL this POST is going to, or find its child spans.
  >

  >

  > 
  > The failed "POST" span in the abnormal trace has NO child spans, which means the HTTP call never reached ts-basic-service (or there's no trace propagation).

  > - error_count: 0
  > - avg_duration_ms: 80.8

  >

  > "send delivery info to mq error][exception: org.springframework.amqp.AmqpIOException: java.net.UnknownHostException: ts-rabbitmq: Name or service not known"
  > 
  > This is a DNS error for `ts-rabbitmq`. The ts-food-service can't resolve `ts-rabbitmq`. But this is about food service and rabbitmq, not directly related to the main incident.
  > 
  > But wait - could there be a DNS issue affecting the entire cluster? If ts-food-service can't resolve ts-rabbitmq by name, maybe other services are also having DNS issues? Like ts-travel-service can't resolve ts-basic-service?
  > 
  > This is getting interesting. The "UnknownHostException" error is a DNS resolution failure. If there's a broader DNS issue in the cluster, it could explain why ts-travel-service's outbound POST calls fail without creating child spans (the call never even gets off the ground because DNS resolution fails).
  > 
  > Let me look at the specific travel-service logs to see if there are DNS errors, or check if there's a service called ts-rabbitmq being looked up.

  > Actually, ts-rabbitmq is an external message broker. It might have been removed or renamed. But the food-service failing to connect to rabbitmq doesn't necessarily mean travel-service has DNS issues.

  {"limit": 30, "parquet_files": ["/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/abnormal_traces.parquet", "/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/normal_traces.parquet"], "query": "\n-- Compare average latency of key services between abnormal and normal\nSELECT \n    t.period,\n    t.service_name,\n    COUNT(*) as total_spans,\n    ROUND(AVG(t.duration)/1000000.0, 2) as avg_ms,\n    ROUND(MAX(t.duration)/1000000.0, 2) as max_ms,\n    PERCENTILE_CONT(0.95) WITHIN GROUP (ORDER BY t.duration) / 1000000.0 as p95_ms\nFROM (\n    SELECT 'abnormal' as period, service_name, duration FROM abnormal_traces\n    WHERE service_name IN ('ts-basic-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-train-service', 'ts-station-service', 'ts-price-service', 'ts-travel-service', 'ts-route-plan-service', 'ts-travel-plan-service')\n    UNION ALL\n    SELECT 'normal' as period, service_name, duration FROM normal_traces\n    WHERE service_name IN ('ts-basic-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-train-service', 'ts-station-service', 'ts-price-service', 'ts-travel-service', 'ts-route-plan-service', 'ts-travel-plan-service')\n) t\nGROUP BY t.period, t.service_name\nORDER BY t.service_name, t.period\n"}

  {"limit": 30, "parquet_files": ["/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/abnormal_metrics_sum.parquet", "/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/normal_metrics_sum.parquet"], "query": "\n-- Compare jvm thread count and memory metrics for key services\nSELECT \n    t.period,\n    t.service_name,\n    t.metric,\n    ROUND(AVG(t.value), 2) as avg_value,\n    ROUND(MAX(t.value), 2) as max_value\nFROM (\n    SELECT 'abnormal' as period, service_name, metric, value FROM abnormal_metrics_sum\n    WHERE metric IN ('jvm.thread.count', 'jvm.memory.used', 'jvm.cpu.time')\n    AND service_name IN ('ts-basic-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-train-service', 'ts-travel-service', 'ts-route-plan-service', 'ts-travel-plan-service', 'ts-travel2-service')\n    UNION ALL\n    SELECT 'normal' as period, service_name, metric, value FROM normal_metrics_sum\n    WHERE metric IN ('jvm.thread.count', 'jvm.memory.used', 'jvm.cpu.time')\n    AND service_name IN ('ts-basic-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-train-service', 'ts-travel-service', 'ts-route-plan-service', 'ts-travel-plan-service', 'ts-travel2-service')\n) t\nGROUP BY t.period, t.service_name, t.metric\nHAVING AVG(t.value) > 0\nORDER BY t.metric, t.service_name, t.period\n"}

- think_tool:
  > Excellent! Now I have key evidence:
  > 
  > 1. **ts-route-plan-service SEVERE error logs**: 
  >    - "Servlet.service() for servlet [dispatcherServlet] threw exception [Request processing failed; nested exception is org.springframework.web.client.HttpServerErrorException$InternalServerError: 500 Internal Server Error: [{"timestamp":"2025-07-19T13:43:42.949+00:00","status":500,"error":"Internal Server Error","message":"","path":"/api/v1/travelservice/trips/left"}]] with root cause"

  {"limit": 40, "parquet_files": ["/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/abnormal_metrics_histogram.parquet", "/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/normal_metrics_histogram.parquet"], "query": "\n-- Compare GC metrics between abnormal and normal periods\nSELECT \n    t.period,\n    t.service_name,\n    t.metric,\n    t.attr_jvm_gc_name,\n    ROUND(AVG(t.sum), 2) as avg_gc_sum,\n    ROUND(MAX(t.sum), 2) as max_gc_sum,\n    ROUND(AVG(t.count), 2) as avg_gc_count,\n    ROUND(MAX(t.count), 2) as max_gc_count\nFROM (\n    SELECT 'abnormal' as period, service_name, metric, attr_jvm_gc_name, sum, count FROM abnormal_metrics_histogram\n    WHERE metric LIKE '%jvm.gc%'\n    UNION ALL\n    SELECT 'normal' as period, service_name, metric, attr_jvm_gc_name, sum, count FROM normal_metrics_histogram\n    WHERE metric LIKE '%jvm.gc%'\n) t\nGROUP BY t.period, t.service_name, t.metric, t.attr_jvm_gc_name\nORDER BY t.service_name, t.metric, t.period\nLIMIT 40\n"}

  > 1. ts-travel-service returns 500 on /api/v1/travelservice/trips/left
  > 2. The ts-travel-service fails to call ts-basic-service (POST span with ERROR and no children)
  > 3. ts-basic-service calls ts-route-service, ts-train-service, ts-price-service - all of which show elevated latency
  > 4. The elevated latency in downstream services is likely causing ts-basic-service to be slow
  > 5. And ts-travel-service's call to ts-basic-service is failing/timing out
  > 
  > But WAIT - why does ts-travel-service's POST call to ts-basic-service show up as ERROR with NO child spans? If ts-basic-service was just slow (taking 5 seconds), the ts-travel-service would either wait (and eventually get a 200 with high latency) or timeout with a 500.
  > 
  > The fact that there are NO child spans from ts-basic-service in the error traces suggests ts-travel-service's call NEVER reached ts-basic-service. This would happen if:
  > 1. Connection refused (ts-basic-service is down - but it has 1151 spans so it's not completely down)

  > 
  > But in other traces, ts-travel-service successfully calls ts-basic-service. The question is: why does it fail in some cases?
  > 
  > I think what might be happening is: ts-travel-service has a connection pool or circuit breaker mechanism. When it receives too many slow requests, it starts failing fast (returning 500 without even trying to call ts-basic-service).
  > 
  > OR: There might be specific conditions under which ts-basic-service is unavailable. For example, if ts-basic-service is doing a long GC pause, during that GC pause, all incoming connections to ts-basic-service would timeout/fail.
  >

  ```
  {"limit": 30, "parquet_files": ["/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/abnormal_metrics.parquet", "/home/nn/SOTA-agents/RCAgentEval/eval-data/thinkdepthai-claude-sonnet-4.6/data_1635f7e7/normal_metrics.parquet"], "query": "\n-- Compare jvm.system.cpu.utilization between abnormal and normal\nSELECT \n    t.period,\n    t.service_name,\n    t.attr_k8s_node_name,\n    ROUND(AVG(t.value), 4) as avg_sys_cpu,\n    ROUND(MAX(t.value), 4) as max_sys_cpu\nFROM (\n    SELECT 'abnormal' as period, service_name, attr_k8s_node_name, value \n    FROM abnormal_metrics\n    WHERE metric = 'jvm.system.cpu.utilization'\n    AND attr_k8s_node_name IS NOT NULL AND attr_k8s_node_name != ''\n    UNION ALL\n    SELECT 'normal' as period, service_name, attr_k8s_node_name, value \n    FROM normal_metrics\n    WHERE metric = 'jvm.system.cpu.utilization'\n    AND attr_k8s_node_name IS NOT NULL AND attr_k8s_node_name != ''\n) t\nWHERE service_name IN ('ts-train-service', 'ts-route-service', 'ts-price-service', 'ts-basic-service', 'ts-travel-service', 'ts-travel-plan-service', 'ts-admin-user-service')\nGROUP BY t.period, t.service_name, t.attr_k8s_node_name\nORDER BY t.attr_k8s_node_name, t.service_name, t.period\n"}
  ```

  > Hmm, this suggests that the jvm.system.cpu.utilization metric is not purely the node-level CPU - there might be some other processes (system services, Kubernetes infrastructure) that are consuming CPU on these nodes.
  > 
  > BUT the key finding from worker5: **ts-verification-code-service** has max CPU of 1.967 (nearly 2 CPUs!) in the abnormal period! This is the highest CPU usage of any service!
  > 
  > And ts-verification-code-service was on the same node (worker5) as ts-station-service. But ts-station-service has 1232 WARN messages... wait, no - the WARN messages were for ts-verification-code-service (they were about "Cookie not found").
  > 
  > Now looking at the workers:
  > - worker1: ts-admin-user-service has 107x CPU increase (max 0.859)
  > - worker2: ts-order-other-service has 3.2x CPU increase (max 1.052!)
  > - worker4: ts-travel-service has similar CPU but system CPU is high
  > - worker5: **ts-verification-code-service** has 7.7x CPU increase (max **1.967**!!)
  > - worker6: ts-basic-service and other services have LOWER CPU
  > 
  > Wait wait wait. ts-verification-code-service on worker5 has max CPU of 1.967! This is by far the highest. But it's on worker5, where ts-station-service is also running.
  > 
  > Let me look at what ts-verification-code-service does - it's for authentication/login. The 1232 WARN messages about "Cookie not found" might be causing it to spin in a loop trying to verify cookies.
  > 
  > But ts-station-service on worker5 shows LOWER CPU in abnormal period, and ts-station-service has 2.3x higher average latency in abnormal traces. That doesn't quite fit the "CPU starvation" model from ts-verification-code-service.
  > 
  > Let me reconsider the overall picture:
  > 
  > Looking at ALL anomalous CPU containers:
  > 1. ts-verification-code-service (worker5): max 1.967 CPUs (7.7x increase!)
  > 2. ts-order-other-service (worker2): max 1.052 CPUs (3.2x increase)
  > 3. ts-admin-user-service (worker1): max 0.859 CPUs (107x increase from near-zero)
  > 4. ts-train-service (worker1): max 0.979 CPUs (6x increase) - SYMPTOM
  > 5. ts-travel-plan-service (worker1): max 0.863 CPUs (4.7x increase) - SYMPTOM
  > 
  > And ts-verification-code-service has 1232 WARN messages about "Cookie not found".
  > 
  > Actually, looking at the logs: ts-verification-code-service WARN messages: 616 "Cookie not found" + individual "Code not found" messages. The 616 "Cookie not found" messages is high. If the service is repeatedly failing to find cookies and retrying, it could burn CPU.
  > 
  > But ts-verification-code-service is on worker5 with ts-station-service. ts-station-service shows:
  > - avg latency 8.9ms → 20.31ms (2.3x increase)
  > - max latency 3578ms → 4774ms
  > 
  > And ts-station-service CPU went from 0.133 to 0.033 (LOWER!). This is actually LESS CPU usage in abnormal. The station service is doing LESS work (receiving fewer requests due to upstream failures).
  > 
  > OK, I'm going to step back and reassess:
  > 
  > **Revised Root Cause Analysis:**
  > 
  > The MOST significant individual anomalies (container CPU):
  > 1. **ts-verification-code-service** (worker5): max CPU 1.967 (7.7x increase)
  > 2. **ts-order-other-service** (worker2): max CPU 1.052 (3.2x increase)  
  > 3. **ts-admin-user-service** (worker1): max CPU 0.859 (107x increase from near-zero)
  > 
  > But these services are NOT directly in the call chain of the failing endpoints:
  > - ts-verification-code-service: handles login/cookie verification
  > - ts-order-other-service: handles order queries
  > - ts-admin-user-service: handles admin user operations
  > 
  > These services could be the "noisy neighbors" but not direct causes of the request failures.
  > 
  > Actually wait - could the elevated CPU across the entire cluster be explained by ALL of these high-CPU containers simultaneously?
  > 
  > Let me think about the system-level CPU on each node:
  > - worker1 system CPU: 0.164 → 0.443. The high CPU services are ts-admin-user-service (0.859 max) + ts-train-service (0.979 max). These could together cause high system CPU.
  > - worker2 system CPU: 0.090 → 0.353. ts-order-other-service (1.052 max) + ts-auth-service (1.323 max, consistent in both periods) could explain this.
  > - worker5 system CPU: would be ts-verification-code-service (1.967 max!)
  > 
  > For worker4 and worker6 - the system CPU is elevated but no individual container shows a clear spike. Could be network or Kubernetes infrastructure.
  > 
  > OK, now I'm going to make my final call. The pattern suggests:
  > 
  > 1. Multiple services are experiencing high CPU simultaneously (ts-verification-code-service, ts-order-other-service, ts-admin-user-service)
  > 2. The high CPU on these services causes CPU contention on their respective nodes
  > 3. This causes slow processing for co-located services (ts-train-service on worker1 due to ts-admin-user-service)
  > 4. The elevated system load causes GC pauses across JVMs
  > 
  > But the KEY question: which single service INITIATED the failure chain?
  > 
  > Looking at the FAILURE TRACE:
  > - ts-travel-service returns 500 (calls ts-basic-service which fails to aggregate)
  > - ts-basic-service aggregates ts-route-service + ts-train-service + ts-station-service + ts-price-service
  > - All these downstream services are slow
  > - The slowness is due to elevated CPU pressure on their nodes
  > 
  > The most dramatic individual anomaly is ts-admin-user-service (107x CPU increase). But ts-verification-code-service has the highest absolute CPU (1.967 CPUs!).
  > 
  > Actually, wait - I haven't checked yet: what is the normal CPU of ts-verification-code-service? It's:
  > - Normal: avg 0.071, max 0.255
  > - Abnormal: avg 0.247 (3.5x), max 1.967 (7.7x!)
  > 
  > And it's on worker5 with ts-station-service. ts-station-service shows elevated latency (2.3x). Could ts-verification-code-service's CPU spike be causing ts-station-service to be slow? If so:
  > - ts-verification-code-service (worker5) → CPU starvation → ts-station-service slow
  > - ts-station-service is called by ts-basic-service
  > - ts-basic-service gets slow
  > - etc.
  > 
  > But ts-station-service also connects to MySQL (on worker1), so the ts-admin-user-service → MySQL slowness also affects ts-station-service.
  > 
  > **CONCLUSION:**
  > 
  > After thorough analysis, the root cause is **most likely** the cluster-wide CPU pressure caused by multiple "noisy neighbor" services running at high CPU simultaneously:
  > 1. **ts-admin-user-service** (worker1): most dramatic RELATIVE increase (107x from near-zero), same node as MySQL
  > 2. **ts-verification-code-service** (worker5): highest absolute CPU (1.967 CPUs max)
  > 
  > However, given that:
  > - ts-admin-user-service shares a node with MySQL (the shared DB for all services)
  > - ts-admin-user-service's CPU spike would directly impact MySQL's performance
  > - MySQL slowness would affect ALL services on ALL nodes
  > 
  > I'll go with **ts-admin-user-service** as the primary root cause, with the propagation being through MySQL performance degradation.
  > 
  > Actually, let me reconsider one more time. The ts-train-service's TrainTypeRepository.findByName shows a 12.7x latency increase. But the SELECT ts.train_type query shows only 2.2x increase. The gap (12.7x vs 2.2x) is much larger than what MySQL CPU contention would cause. This suggests either:
  > 
  > 1. ts-train-service's own JVM is struggling to process results (CPU starvation from ts-admin-user-service on same node)
  > 2. JDBC connection pool contention
  > 
  > Since ts-train-service is on worker1 WITH ts-admin-user-service, the CPU starvation of ts-train-service's JVM (not MySQL) is the more likely explanation for the 12.7x latency in the repository method.
  > 
  > So the propagation is:
  > 1. ts-admin-user-service HIGH_CPU on worker1
  > 2. → ts-train-service (worker1) CPU starved → HIGH_LATENCY in TrainTypeRepository.findByName
  > 3. → Also, ts-train-service's own GC takes longer (1.7x) due to CPU contention
  > 4. → ts-basic-service (worker6) aggregates slow responses → HIGH_LATENCY
  > 5. → ts-travel-service (worker4) calls ts-basic-service and fails/times out → HIGH_ERROR_RATE
  > 
  > But that still doesn't explain ts-route-service and ts-price-service (worker2) being slow. They're not on worker1.
  > 
  > So there must be ANOTHER cause for worker2 slowness. The most likely candidate is:
  > - MySQL on worker1 being slow (affecting ts-route-service's DB queries via network)
  > - ts-order-other-service on worker2 consuming high CPU
  > 
  > I think both factors are contributing. The primary root cause is ts-admin-user-service (most anomalous, 107x CPU increase), but ts-order-other-service (worker2) might be a secondary factor affecting ts-route-service and ts-price-service.
  > 
  > For the RCA output, I'll present ts-admin-user-service as the root cause with HIGH_CPU state, and show the propagation chain.
  > 
  > Actually, I realize there might be one more thing to consider. Let me look at whether there are any network issues (hubble_drop_total by specific pod) that might explain ts-route-service being slow on worker2. But I've already checked that and the drops weren't dramatically different.
  > 
  > OK, FINAL DECISION:
  > 
  > **Root Cause**: ts-admin-user-service (HIGH_CPU state) on worker1
  > - Causes CPU contention on worker1, affecting ts-train-service and ts-travel-plan-service
  > - Causes MySQL degradation (MySQL is also on worker1), affecting DB queries across all services
  > 
  > **Propagation**:
  > 1. ts-admin-user-service HIGH_CPU → MySQL HIGH_LATENCY
  > 2. MySQL HIGH_LATENCY → ts-train-service HIGH_LATENCY (also direct CPU contention on worker1)
  > 3. MySQL HIGH_LATENCY → ts-route-service HIGH_LATENCY (DB queries via network)
  > 4. MySQL HIGH_LATENCY → ts-price-service HIGH_LATENCY
  > 5. MySQL HIGH_LATENCY → ts-station-service HIGH_LATENCY
  > 6. ts-train-service + ts-route-service + ts-price-service + ts-station-service HIGH_LATENCY → ts-basic-service HIGH_LATENCY
  > 7. ts-basic-service HIGH_LATENCY → ts-travel-service HIGH_ERROR_RATE (timeouts)
  > 8. ts-travel-service HIGH_ERROR_RATE → ts-route-plan-service HIGH_ERROR_RATE
  > 9. ts-route-plan-service HIGH_ERROR_RATE → ts-travel-plan-service HIGH_ERROR_RATE
  > 10. ts-route-service HIGH_LATENCY → SLO violation for GET /routeservice/routes
  > 
  > The failing endpoints from the incident are all explained by this chain.
  > 
  > Now let me produce the final causal graph.
